Key Jyotish Terms Used in This Case StudyLagna: The ascendant or rising sign, the zodiac sign on the eastern horizon at the moment of birth. Sets the first house and governs the entire chart structure in Vedic astrology (Jyotish).
Nakshatra: One of 27 lunar mansions in Vedic astrology. Each Nakshatra spans 13 degrees 20 minutes of the zodiac and reveals deeper emotional and karmic patterns beyond the sun or moon sign.
Navamsa (D9): The ninth divisional chart in Jyotish. Used for detailed analysis of marriage, dharma, and the soul's deeper purpose. Considered the most important divisional chart after the D1 Rasi chart.
Vimshottari Dasha: The primary planetary period system in Vedic astrology. A 120 year cycle of planetary rulerships (Mahadasha) and sub periods (Antardasha) used to time life events with precision.
BNN (Bhrigu Nandi Nadi): A branch of Nadi astrology where planets in 5th or 9th relationship are treated as functionally conjunct, combining their energies as powerfully as a direct conjunction.

Frequently Asked Questions
What is Saturn Mahadasha and how does it affect daily life?+Saturn Mahadasha is a 19 year period in the Vimshottari dasha system of Vedic astrology during which Saturn becomes the primary planetary ruler of your life themes. During this period, Saturn's natural karakas, karma, discipline, service, restriction, longevity, and delayed reward, become dominant. For natives with Saturn placed in difficult houses (6th, 8th, 12th), Saturn Mahadasha effects show up as sustained pressure, reduced resources, and confrontation with long suppressed patterns. For those with well placed Saturn it can bring structured, lasting achievement. These effects intensify when a concurrent Saturn transit activates the same houses natally occupied by Saturn.

What does the 12th house mean in Vedic astrology?+The 12th house in Vedic astrology governs endings, liberation (moksha), hidden enemies, foreign lands, bed pleasures, secret karma, isolated retreat, and self undoing. It is one of the most misunderstood houses in Jyotish because it contains both the highest spiritual potential (liberation) and the deepest karmic traps (addiction, hidden destructive patterns). Planets in the 12th house do not operate in the visible world, they work underground. Saturn retrograde in the 12th house specifically indicates past life karma that must be consciously faced during this lifetime, particularly during Saturn Mahadasha and any Saturn transit reinforcing the 12th house theme.

What is Rahu Grasthata in Vedic astrology?+Rahu Grasthata in Vedic astrology translates roughly as Rahu possession, a condition where Rahu's shadowy, obsessive, desire amplifying quality begins to override the native's conscious will and rational judgement. It manifests as intense attraction to something (a person, substance, experience) that the native knows intellectually is harmful but cannot resist emotionally. In the chart it is identified when Rahu conjoins or closely aspects the Sun (identity), Moon (mind), or Mercury (rational thinking), particularly in the 6th, 8th, or 12th houses. The condition is strongest during Rahu's own dasha, its nakshatra lord's dasha, or a Saturn Mahadasha that afflicts the same group.

What is Bahu Manzil Yoga and what does it indicate?+Bahu Manzil Yoga is identified in BNN astrology (Bhrigu Nandi Nadi) when Mars, Venus, and Rahu form a trine or conjunction in the birth chart. Bahu Manzil translates as multiple floors, indicating multiple significant romantic or desire based episodes in the native's life. This yoga amplifies desire, attraction to multiple partners, and a tendency toward relationships that carry karmic weight. In classical Vedic astrology the manifestation depends heavily on the houses involved and the dasha operating: in productive periods it can indicate great passion and creative energy, but during Rahu dasha or Saturn Mahadasha activation it can manifest as obsessive relationships or moral compromise.

How does BNN (Bhrigu Nandi Nadi) differ from classical Vedic astrology?+BNN astrology, also called Bhrigu Nandi Nadi, is a branch of Nadi astrology attributed to the sage Bhrigu's tradition, systematised by R.G. Rao and taught at the K.N. Rao Institute in the modern period. The key methodological difference from classical Parashari Vedic astrology is the treatment of trines: in BNN, planets in 5th and 9th relationship from each other are treated as functionally conjunct, their energies combine as powerfully as if they occupied the same house. BNN also has specific marriage karakas that differ from classical Jyotish: Mars equals 1st husband (for women), not Jupiter. Venus equals 1st wife (for men). These differences significantly change marriage timing and relationship analysis.

Can planetary remedies actually change karma?+Yes, planetary remedies in Jyotish reshape how karma is expressed, though they do not erase the karma itself. In Vedic astrology, karma is not a fixed prison, it is a dialogue. Prarabdha karma (karma already set in motion, indicated by the birth chart) cannot be removed, but its expression can be shaped. Remedies work not by changing planetary positions but by changing the native's internal alignment with those planetary energies. Hanuman worship during Saturn Mahadasha for example does not remove Saturn, it helps the native embody Saturn's highest qualities (discipline, service, patience) rather than its lower ones (restriction, addiction, isolation).

What is the significance of a very late degree ascendant like Aries 29°54'?+A very late degree ascendant (28° to 30°) in Vedic astrology carries the energy of both that sign and the next, the native is simultaneously completing one archetype and beginning another. For Ri**'s Aries 29°54', this means Aries (warrior, initiation, courage) is at its final breath and Taurus (stability, earthiness, material world) is about to begin. Practically, this creates a personality that feels perpetually at a threshold, never quite settled into the identity the rising sign promises. In BNN and classical Jyotish both, this degree is considered significant because the ascendant lord's period (here, Mars) carries particular weight and the native's life direction can shift substantially at key dasha junctions.

Effects, Duration and What to Expect in Each Antardasha
Jun 22, 2026·9 min read·By Saurabh Jain, K.N. Rao Institute

The Short Answer
Saturn Mahadasha is a 19 year karmic phase ruled by Shani in the Vimshottari dasha system. It rewards discipline, structure, and service, and exposes weakness, ego, and shortcuts. The actual result depends entirely on the natal placement of Saturn and its aspects in your chart.

What is Saturn Mahadasha?
In the Vimshottari Mahadasha system, every native passes through nine planetary periods of fixed length. Saturn rules 19 of those years. The Mahadasha begins based on the Moon nakshatra at birth, which is why two people born minutes apart can be at completely different stages.
Saturn is the karaka of time, karma, labor, and patience. When his dasha activates, the chart restructures around what is truly built rather than what is merely wished for. Shortcuts collapse. Solid foundations remain.
The texture of the 19 years is not uniform. Each Antardasha, the sub period within the dasha, brings the flavor of another planet onto Saturn. This is why one Saturn Mahadasha native flourishes while another struggles in the same year.

Sanskrit Mantra
ॐ प्रां प्रीं प्रौं सः शनैश्चराय नमः
Om Praam Preem Praum Sah Shanaischaray Namah
I bow to Saturn, the giver of karma and patience.

The Nine Antardashas of Saturn
Each sub period within Saturn Mahadasha carries the flavor of another planet. The order is fixed but the result depends on the strength of each planet in your natal chart.
Saturn in Saturn
3 yr 0 mo
Foundation
The full Saturnian flavor. Slow progress, hard work, karmic reckoning. Health and bones need care.

Mixed
Business mind sharpens. Communication contracts. Travel and paperwork dominate. Good for steady gains.

Sudden cuts, separations, spiritual openings. Old attachments dissolve. Health check advised.

Material gains, marriage, vehicle, property. Relationship stability if Venus is well placed.

Friction with authority, father, government. Career test. Status pressure. Move with patience.

Mood weight, mother concern, mental fatigue. Sleep and rest matter most in this phase.

Saturn in Mars
1 yr 1 mo

Conflict, accidents, blood pressure, anger. Property disputes possible. Move slowly and safely.

Foreign moves, sudden change, shocks, unconventional choices. Confusion if Rahu is afflicted.

Saturn in Jupiter
2 yr 6 mo
Wisdom
Recovery, dharma return, family, children, guru blessings. Often the most healing antardasha.

Career and Money Under Saturn

Slow but Lasting Growth

Saturn rewards discipline. Promotions feel delayed but become permanent. Job stability over speed.

Karmic Industries Favor You

Iron, oil, mining, real estate, government, law, public service, judiciary. Saturn supports labor based fields.

Avoid Speculation

Stock trading, lottery, and quick schemes typically fail under Saturn. Long term investing succeeds.

Workload Increases

Responsibility grows. Burnout risk is real. Health, sleep, and joints need attention throughout.

Sade Sati vs Saturn Mahadasha
These two Saturnian phases are often confused. They are different mechanisms and need different remedies.

Five Remedies for Saturn Mahadasha
01Chant Shani Beej Mantra 108 times daily
Om Praam Preem Praum Sah Shanaischaray Namah, on a black kala hakik or rudraksha mala, ideally on Saturday.

02Serve elders, laborers, and the underprivileged
Saturn is the karaka of the common man. Feeding workers and the poor reduces Saturnian weight quickly.

03Light a mustard oil lamp under a Peepal tree on Saturday
Especially powerful at sunset. Walk around the tree seven times with hands folded.

04Donate black sesame, mustard oil, iron, or black clothes
Donate on Saturday evening to a person in genuine need. Never in pride, only in service.

05Read Hanuman Chalisa and serve Hanuman ji
Hanuman is the only deity who controls Shani. Daily Chalisa is the simplest and strongest remedy.

## /blog/tarot-card-reading-vedic-astrology
Route: /blog/tarot-card-reading-vedic-astrology
URL: https://www.soulinfinity.space/blog/tarot-card-reading-vedic-astrology
Description: Tarot card reading Vedic astrology integration: how tarot complements jyotish, when to use each, and what a combined consultation reveals.

Tarot Card Reading in Vedic Tradition: How It Complements Jyotish

Tarot card reading vedic astrology integration is one of the more interesting developments in contemporary Indian astrological practice. While tarot originated in Europe and traveled through various mystical traditions, its symbolic depth and capacity to provide moment-specific guidance make it complementary to the structural depth of Vedic Jyotish. This guide explains tarot, how it differs from astrology, and how the two can be used together for comprehensive guidance.

What is Tarot?

Tarot is a system of 78 cards (22 Major Arcana plus 56 Minor Arcana) developed in Europe over the past several centuries. The cards carry symbolic archetypes representing fundamental life forces, situations, and patterns. A tarot reading involves shuffling the cards, drawing a specific spread, and interpreting the cards in their drawn positions.

The Major Arcana represents major life forces and themes (The Fool, The Magician, The High Priestess, and so on through The World). The Minor Arcana is divided into four suits (Cups, Pentacles, Swords, Wands) representing emotions, material life, intellect, and action.

Tarot is not predictive in the deterministic sense; it provides a symbolic mirror of the energetic patterns currently active in a situation. A skilled reader uses the cards to surface insights, choices, and consequences that may not be visible to the questioner.

How Tarot Differs from Vedic Astrology

| Aspect | Tarot | Vedic Astrology |
|---|---|---|
| Foundation | Symbolic archetypes | Planetary positions |
| Time scale | Current moment to short-term future | Lifetime structural patterns |
| Format | Cards drawn in spreads | Calculated chart from birth data |
| Best for | Specific current questions | Long-term timing and patterns |
| Birth data needed | No | Yes (date, time, place) |
| Mechanism | Symbolic intuition | Mathematical and rule-based |
| Tradition | European (with various roots) | Indian classical |

Both are valid traditions with different strengths. Tarot does not need birth data and can be applied to any question immediately. Vedic astrology needs accurate birth data but provides deeper structural insight that tarot cannot.

When to Use Tarot vs Astrology

Use tarot for:

"Should I take this specific job offer?"

"How is this relationship developing right now?"

"What energy is around this decision?"

"Should I have this difficult conversation?"

"What am I not seeing about this situation?"

"How will the next 3 months unfold for this project?"

Use Vedic astrology for:

"What is my dharma?"

"When will I marry?"

"Which career fits my chart?"

"What is my current Mahadasha and Antardasha bringing?"

"What does Sade Sati mean for me?"

"Is this relationship compatible long-term according to our charts?"

"What is the karmic pattern of my family?"

Both systems answer "what should I do" questions, but they answer at different depths and time scales.

A Combined Tarot and Astrology Consultation

At Soul Infinity, many consultations integrate tarot with Vedic astrology. A typical combined session might:

Begin with the birth chart context: which dasha is active, which transits are influencing the question, what the structural pattern is

Move to tarot for the specific moment-question: what energy is around this decision now

Integrate the two: the astrological structure provides the long-term framework; the tarot provides the immediate guidance

Conclude with practical recommendations: what to do, when to act, what to be aware of

The integration is more useful than either alone for clients facing specific decisions within larger life questions.

Tarot for Specific Question Types

Career decisions: A 5-card spread covering present situation, what is supporting, what is blocking, the likely outcome, and the wisdom to apply. The Major Arcana cards in this spread often indicate the deeper karmic theme.

Relationships: A 7-card spread covering your energy, partner's energy, the connection, what is supporting, what is challenging, the near-term direction, the wisdom to apply.

Specific decisions: A 3-card spread (past, present, future) or 5-card spread for more nuance.

Spiritual questions: A single card or simple spread focusing on the current guidance available.

The reading is most useful when the question is clear and focused. Vague questions produce vague guidance.

What to Expect in a Tarot Session

Pre-session: You identify the question or area you want to explore. The clearer the question, the more focused the reading.

The reading: The reader (Saurabh Jain) shuffles the deck while focusing on your question, then draws cards in a specific spread. The cards are interpreted in their positions, with attention to the relationships between cards.

Discussion: The reader explains what the cards reveal and helps you integrate the insights with your specific situation.

Action items: The reading concludes with practical guidance: what to do, what to be aware of, what to avoid.

A typical tarot session runs 45 to 60 minutes for a single focused question, or 75 to 90 minutes for multiple questions or combined tarot-astrology work.

The Reader's Role

Tarot accuracy depends significantly on the reader's skill. A skilled tarot reader:

Has trained extensively in the tarot symbolism and spreads

Combines intuitive perception with knowledge of the cards

Focuses fully during the reading without distraction

Is honest about what the cards show, even when difficult

Empowers the client rather than creating dependency

Knows when to refer to other modalities (such as Vedic astrology) for the deeper picture

At Soul Infinity, tarot is practiced as a serious guidance tradition, not as entertainment or fortune-telling.

Common Misconceptions About Tarot

"Tarot predicts the future." Tarot reveals current energetic patterns and likely directions; it does not predict deterministic outcomes. Free will and conscious action change outcomes.

"Some cards are always bad." Cards like Death, Tower, or Devil have intense imagery but their meaning depends on the question and position. The Death card often represents transformation, not literal death. The Tower represents necessary breakdown of false structure.

"You should never read your own cards." Self-reading is possible but more difficult because of the practitioner's emotional involvement. Many tarot readers prefer to work with another reader for their own significant questions.

"Tarot conflicts with Hinduism." Many serious tarot practitioners integrate the tradition with Vedic and Indian spirituality without conflict. The card symbolism is universal enough to translate across traditions.

Booking a Tarot Reading

For a tarot reading at Soul Infinity, with or without integrated Vedic astrology, contact us through WhatsApp. Mention your question or focus area so we can prepare appropriately.

## /blog/theta-healing-vs-reiki
Route: /blog/theta-healing-vs-reiki
URL: https://www.soulinfinity.space/blog/theta-healing-vs-reiki
Description: Theta healing vs Reiki: how each modality works, what they treat, and how to choose between them based on your needs and chart.

Theta Healing vs Reiki: Two Energy Modalities Compared

Theta Healing vs Reiki is a question that arises when clients explore energy modalities beyond Reiki, which is by far the most widely known. Theta Healing is newer but has gained substantial traction worldwide, particularly for belief-based work. This guide explains both modalities, their distinct mechanisms, what each is best suited for, and how they can be combined for layered work.

What is Theta Healing?

Theta Healing is a meditative healing technique developed by Vianna Stibal in the 1990s. The system uses a specific guided meditation to bring the practitioner and client into the theta brain wave state, the deeply relaxed state associated with deep meditation, light sleep, and the subconscious mind.

In this state, the practitioner guides the client to identify limiting beliefs (about money, love, worth, health, possibility) and then to replace them with empowering beliefs through a process called digging and downloading. The premise is that subconscious beliefs drive much of our experience, and changing these beliefs at the theta level produces lasting shifts in life patterns.

A Theta Healing session typically involves:

Establishing the theta state through guided meditation

Identifying the limiting belief the client wants to address

Tracing the belief back to its origin (often in childhood or ancestral patterns)

Witnessing the belief change at the subconscious level

Downloading new beliefs that replace the old patterns

Integration through breathing and body awareness

What is Reiki?

Reiki is a Japanese energy healing system developed by Mikao Usui in the early 20th century. It channels universal life force energy through the practitioner's hands to support the recipient's natural healing processes. (See our complete Reiki vs Pranic Healing guide for full Reiki background.)

A Reiki session involves the client resting fully clothed while the practitioner places hands lightly on or just above specific body areas in a sequence. The session is meditative, often producing deep relaxation or light sleep, and works on the energetic level without specific belief content.

Key Methodological Differences

| Aspect | Theta Healing | Reiki |
|---|---|---|
| Origin | Vianna Stibal, 1990s | Mikao Usui, 1920s |
| Mechanism | Belief change at theta brain wave | Energy channeling through practitioner |
| Focus | Subconscious belief patterns | Energy field and chakras |
| Activity | Interactive (client and practitioner dialogue) | Passive (client receives) |
| Touch | Light touch or no touch | Hands-on or hands-near |
| Session structure | Belief identification and reprogramming | Sequential hand positions |
| Best for | Specific belief work | General energy balance |
| Verbal content | Significant verbal exchange | Minimal verbal exchange |

The most significant difference is that Theta Healing is interactive and belief-focused, while Reiki is more passive and energy-focused.

Which is Better for Different Conditions?

Choose Theta Healing when:

You have identified specific limiting beliefs you want to change

You are doing work on money beliefs, relationship beliefs, or worth beliefs

You are exploring ancestral patterns that affect current life

You want to participate actively in your healing

You are open to discussing childhood experiences and family patterns

Choose Reiki when:

You want deep relaxation and stress relief

You are recovering from illness, surgery, or grief

You prefer a passive, receptive experience

You want general energy balancing without specific belief work

You are processing trauma and need gentle, non-verbal support

For natives with strong Moon afflictions (anxiety, mood patterns, attachment difficulties), Theta Healing can produce specific belief shifts that complement astrological remedies.

For natives in Sade Sati or difficult Saturn periods, Reiki provides the steady energetic support that helps maintain balance.

How to Combine Theta and Reiki

Many practitioners trained in both modalities integrate them in a layered approach:

Opening: Brief Reiki to establish energetic balance and bring the client into a relaxed, receptive state. This is typically 10-15 minutes.

Core work: Theta Healing on the specific belief or pattern the client wants to address. This is typically 30-45 minutes and involves verbal dialogue.

Integration: Closing Reiki to support the body and energy field in absorbing the changes. This is typically 10-15 minutes.

A 90-minute integrated session covers both modalities and tends to produce more lasting results than either alone.

Integration with Vedic Astrology

At Soul Infinity, both modalities are integrated with Vedic astrology to address the karmic and energetic roots of the issues being worked on.

The chart reveals:

Which areas of life carry the most karmic intensity

Which planets are afflicted and what kind of energetic support they need

Which dasha periods activate which themes

Which remedies (mantras, gemstones, ritual practice) complement energy work

A Moon-afflicted native may benefit from Reiki for emotional regulation and Theta Healing for specific beliefs about worthiness or being loved. A Mars-afflicted native may benefit from Pranic Healing for anger patterns and Theta Healing for beliefs about safety and aggression. A Saturn-afflicted native may benefit from Reiki for low energy and Theta Healing for beliefs about scarcity and limitation.

What to Expect in a Session

A typical session at Soul Infinity covers:

Brief astrological context (10 minutes): the relevant planetary indications

Reiki opening (15 minutes): energetic balancing

Theta Healing work (40 minutes): specific belief change

Reiki closing (15 minutes): integration

Brief discussion (10 minutes): what to do between sessions

Sessions typically run 90 minutes. Multiple sessions are recommended for deeper belief patterns.

Booking a Session

To book a Theta Healing, Reiki, or integrated session, contact Soul Infinity through WhatsApp. Mention your specific concerns so we can recommend the right modality or combination.

## /blog/what-is-bnn-astrology-explained
Route: /blog/what-is-bnn-astrology-explained
URL: https://www.soulinfinity.space/blog/what-is-bnn-astrology-explained
Description: BNN astrology (Bhrigu Nandi Nadi) explained: what it is, how it differs from Parashari Jyotish, and why nadi astrology produces such precise predictions.

What is BNN Astrology? Bhrigu Nandi Nadi Explained for Beginners

BNN astrology, short for Bhrigu Nandi Nadi astrology, is one of the most precise predictive systems within the broader Vedic Jyotish tradition. While the main Parashari Jyotish system uses houses, aspects, and Vimshottari dasha, BNN uses a distinct set of tools centered on planetary conjunctions, the Karaka system, and predictive sutras (formulas) preserved in palm-leaf manuscripts. The combination of these tools produces event-level precision that is rare in any astrological tradition.

This guide explains what bhrigu nandi nadi astrology is, how it differs from the main Vedic tradition, what kind of predictions it produces, and what to expect in a BNN consultation.

What is BNN Astrology?

BNN astrology is a specialized predictive system attributed to Sage Bhrigu, one of the seven great sages (saptarishis) of Vedic tradition, and elaborated through the Nandi lineage of South Indian palm-leaf astrology. The system is preserved in ancient palm-leaf manuscripts (nadi granthas) that contain specific predictive sutras applied to individual horoscopes.

The bhrigu nandi nadi astrology approach differs from the standard Vedic system in several ways:

The focus is on event prediction rather than personality analysis

The tools are sutras (formulas) applied to planetary conjunctions and Karaka (significator) positions

The system does not rely as heavily on Vimshottari dasha as Parashari does

Predictions tend to be more specific about timing of events

BNN vs Parashari Astrology

To understand BNN, it helps to compare it with the main Vedic system:

| Aspect | Parashari Jyotish | Bhrigu Nandi Nadi |
|---|---|---|
| Foundation | Brihat Parashara Hora Shastra | Palm-leaf nadi granthas |
| Main tools | Houses, aspects, dasha | Conjunctions, Karakas, sutras |
| Timing system | Vimshottari dasha | Karaka movements and conjunctions |
| Focus | Comprehensive analysis | Event-specific prediction |
| Personality | Strong tool | Less emphasis |
| Precise event timing | Possible with effort | Native strength |
| Remedies | Detailed by ascendant | Karmic and karaka-based |

Neither system is superior. They are complementary, and a trained Jyotishi often uses both: Parashari for the comprehensive picture, BNN for specific event timing and karmic insight.

The Karaka System in BNN

The Karaka system is central to BNN. A Karaka is a planetary significator for specific life themes:

Sun: Father, soul, government, vitality

Moon: Mother, mind, emotions, public popularity

Mars: Brothers, real estate, courage, accidents

Mercury: Maternal relatives, business, intellect, communication

Jupiter: Husband (in female chart), children, dharma, teachers

Venus: Wife (in male chart), marriage, vehicles, comforts

Saturn: Profession, longevity, servants, chronic conditions

Rahu: Father (alternate), foreign matters, unconventional gains

Ketu: Mother (alternate), spirituality, hidden enemies

BNN analyzes the positions of these Karakas, their conjunctions, and their movements through the chart to predict specific events. For example, the conjunction of the Karaka for spouse (Venus or Jupiter depending on gender) with the Karaka for marriage timing can predict the year of marriage with surprising precision.

How BNN Produces Precise Predictions

The precision of BNN comes from several methodological strengths:

1. Specific sutras: The palm-leaf texts contain thousands of specific predictive formulas. When a chart matches a sutra, the predicted outcome is highly reliable.

2. Karaka conjunctions: When two relevant Karakas conjoin in transit or in dasha activation, specific events tend to manifest with the predicted timing.

3. Independent confirmation: BNN does not rely on a single tool. The same prediction is checked through multiple sutras, multiple Karaka assessments, and convergent indicators. Predictions that pass multiple tests are highly reliable.

4. Karmic context: BNN integrates karmic understanding from the palm-leaf tradition. Predictions are not just mechanical but contextualized within the larger soul journey, which helps explain why certain events happen.

What BNN Can Predict

A skilled BNN practitioner can produce predictions about:

Timing of marriage with year-level (sometimes month-level) accuracy

Career events: promotion, business establishment, career change

Foreign travel: when, where, what kind

Property acquisition or sale

Children: timing of conception and birth

Major financial events: gains, losses, inheritance

Health transitions and longevity indicators

Karmic patterns from previous lifetimes that affect current life themes

The level of precision varies by chart. Some natives have charts that respond strongly to BNN analysis; others are better read with combined BNN-Parashari approach.

Nadi Astrology Online

Nadi astrology online consultations are entirely possible when the practitioner is properly trained and has accurate birth data. The principles of BNN do not require physical presence. The required inputs are:

Exact date of birth

Exact time of birth (within 5 minutes ideally)

Exact place of birth (city and country)

The questions or life themes you want addressed

The output is the same quality whether delivered in person, by video call, or in written form. The key variable is the practitioner's training, not the medium of delivery.

What to Expect in a BNN Consultation

A typical BNN consultation at Soul Infinity covers:

Chart casting: Your birth chart is cast with both Parashari and BNN frames.

Karaka analysis: The Karakas relevant to your specific questions are identified and analyzed.

Sutra application: Relevant sutras from the palm-leaf tradition are applied to your chart.

Event prediction: Specific events with their timing are identified for the next several years.

Karmic context: The deeper karmic patterns underlying the events are explained.

Remedies: Karaka-based remedies and karmic practices are recommended.

A BNN consultation typically runs 75 to 90 minutes for a thorough analysis. The output is a detailed reading covering specific predictions for the next 2 to 5 years.

Who Should Consider BNN

BNN is particularly valuable when you want:

Year-level timing for marriage, children, career

Understanding of karmic patterns affecting your life

Confirmation or refinement of Parashari predictions

Insight into specific events rather than general personality

A consultation that integrates classical Indian wisdom with practical guidance

Saurabh Jain at Soul Infinity is trained in both Parashari and BNN traditions through K.N. Rao Institute. A BNN consultation integrates both approaches for the most precise and contextualized analysis.

Booking a BNN Consultation

To book a BNN astrology consultation, contact Soul Infinity through WhatsApp with your birth details (date, time, place) and the questions or life themes you want addressed. We will confirm timing and provide preparation guidance before the session.
